<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Betty White</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>Betty Marion White Ludden</b> (born January 17, 1922)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BiographyCom_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-BiographyCom-2">[2]</a></sup> is an American actress, with the longest television career of a female entertainer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Regarded as a pioneer of television, she was one of the first women to have control both in front of and behind the camera;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> and is recognized as the first woman to produce a sitcom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> which contributed to her receiving the honorary title <i>Mayor of Hollywood</i> in 1955.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>She is known for her <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a>-winning roles as <a href="/wiki/Sue_Ann_Nivens" title="Sue Ann Nivens">Sue Ann Nivens</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show" title="The Mary Tyler Moore Show">The Mary Tyler Moore Show</a></i> (1973–77) and <a href="/wiki/Rose_Nylund" title="Rose Nylund">Rose Nylund</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Golden_Girls" title="The Golden Girls">The Golden Girls</a></i> (1985–92). The <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">Writers Guild of America</a> has included both <a href="/wiki/Sitcom" title="Sitcom">sitcoms</a> in its list of the 101 Best Written TV Series Of All Time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> A staple guest of many American game shows such as <i><a href="/wiki/Password_(game_show)" title="Password (game show)">Password</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Match_Game" title="Match Game">Match Game</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pyramid_(game_show)" title="Pyramid (game show)">The $25,000 Pyramid</a></i>, White has been dubbed the 'First Lady of Game Shows' and became the first woman to receive an Emmy Award for <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Game_Show_Host" title="Daytime Emmy Award for Outstanding Game Show Host">Outstanding Game Show Host</a> in 1983 for the show <i><a href="/wiki/Just_Men!" title="Just Men!">Just Men!</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> From 2010 to 2015, she starred as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elka_Ostrovsky" title="Elka Ostrovsky">Elka Ostrovsky</a> in the <a href="/wiki/TV_Land" title="TV Land">TV Land</a> sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Hot_in_Cleveland" title="Hot in Cleveland">Hot in Cleveland</a></i>, for which she has won two consecutive <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award" title="Screen Actors Guild Award">Screen Actors Guild Awards</a> and she was nominated for an Emmy Award.</p>
<p>In a career that has spanned more than 75<span class="nowrap"> </span>years, she has received seven Emmy awards, three <a href="/wiki/American_Comedy_Awards" title="American Comedy Awards">American Comedy Awards</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a> awards, and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy" title="Grammy">Grammy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> She also has a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>, is a <a href="/wiki/Television_Hall_of_Fame" title="Television Hall of Fame">Television Hall of Fame</a> inductee (class of 1995), and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney_Legend" title="Disney Legend">Disney Legend</a> (class of 2009).</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Betty Marion White was born in <a href="/wiki/Oak_Park,_Illinois" title="Oak Park, Illinois">Oak Park, Illinois</a>, on January 17, 1922.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BiographyCom_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-BiographyCom-2">[2]</a></sup> She has stated that her legal name is Betty and not a shortened version of Elizabeth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shemadeit_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-shemadeit-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inside_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Inside-12">[12]</a></sup> She is the only child of Christine Tess (<a href="/wiki/Given_name#Name_at_birth" title="Given name">née</a> Cachikis; July 25, 1899 – November 11, 1985), a homemaker, and Horace Logan White (May 30, 1899 – November 16, 1963),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> a lighting company executive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Her paternal grandfather was Danish and her maternal grandfather was Greek, with her other roots being English and Welsh (both of her grandmothers were Canadian).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kan_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-kan-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pressbur_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-pressbur-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> White's family moved to <a href="/wiki/Alhambra,_California" title="Alhambra, California">Alhambra, California</a> and later to Los Angeles, during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNL2010_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-SNL2010-20">[20]</a></sup> To make extra money, her father would build radios and sell them wherever he could. Since it was the height of the Depression, and hardly anyone had a sizable income, he would trade the radios in exchange for dogs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Betty.27s_Early_Life_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Betty.27s_Early_Life-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>She attended <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horace_Mann_School_Beverly_Hills" title="Horace Mann School Beverly Hills">Horace Mann School Beverly Hills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills_High_School" title="Beverly Hills High School">Beverly Hills High School</a> and aspired to become a forest ranger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Betty.27s_Early_Life_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Betty.27s_Early_Life-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forest_Ranger_Betty_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forest_Ranger_Betty-22">[22]</a></sup> However, women weren't allowed to become rangers during this time. Instead, White pursued an interest in writing. She wrote and played the lead in a graduation play at Horace Mann School and discovered her interest in performing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aatinterview_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-aatinterview-1">[1]</a></sup> This is where she decided to become an actress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_career">Entertainment career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1940s">1940s</span></h3>
<p>White made rounds to movie studios looking for work, but was always turned down because she was "unphotogenic". So then she started to look for radio jobs where being photogenic did not matter. Her first radio jobs included reading commercials and playing bit parts, and sometimes even doing crowd noises. She made about five dollars a show. She would do just about anything, like singing on a show for no money, or making an appearance on the local game show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>White began her television career in 1939, three months after high school graduation, when she and a classmate sang songs from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Merry_Widow" title="The Merry Widow">The Merry Widow</a></i> on an <a href="/wiki/History_of_television#United_States" title="History of television">experimental Los Angeles channel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aatinterview_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-aatinterview-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneil20100617_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-oneil20100617-24">[24]</a></sup> White found work modeling, and her first professional acting job was at the Bliss Hayden Little Theatre. White's career was disrupted immediately, as World War II broke out, causing her to join the <a href="/wiki/American_Women%27s_Voluntary_Services" title="American Women's Voluntary Services">American Women's Voluntary Services</a>.</p>
<p>In the 1940s, she worked in radio, appearing on shows such as <i><a href="/wiki/Blondie_(radio)" title="Blondie (radio)">Blondie</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Gildersleeve" title="The Great Gildersleeve">The Great Gildersleeve</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/This_is_Your_FBI" title="This is Your FBI">This is Your FBI</a></i>. She then got her own radio show, called <i>The Betty White Show</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1949, she began appearing as co-host with Al Jarvis on his daily <a href="/wiki/Live_television" title="Live television">live television</a> variety show <i><a href="/wiki/Hollywood_on_Television" title="Hollywood on Television">Hollywood on Television</a></i>, originally called <i>Al Jarvis' Make-Believe Ballroom</i> on <a href="/wiki/KFWB" title="KFWB">KFWB radio</a> and on <a href="/wiki/KCOP-TV" title="KCOP-TV">KLAC-TV</a> in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneil20100617_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-oneil20100617-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950s">1950s</span></h3>
<p>White began hosting the show by herself in 1952 after Jarvis' departure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> spanning five and a half hours of live <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ad-lib" title="Ad-lib">ad-lib</a> television six days per week over a contiguous four-year span altogether. In all of her various variety series over the years, White would sing at least a couple of songs during each broadcast. In 1951, she was nominated for her first <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> as "Best Actress" on television, competing with such legendary stars as <a href="/wiki/Judith_Anderson" title="Judith Anderson">Judith Anderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helen_Hayes" title="Helen Hayes">Helen Hayes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Imogene_Coca" title="Imogene Coca">Imogene Coca</a> (the award went to <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Berg" title="Gertrude Berg">Gertrude Berg</a>). This was the very first award and category in the new Emmy history designated for women on television.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_in_The_Betty_White_Show_1954_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="629" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Betty_White_in_The_Betty_White_Show_1954_%282%29.jpg/220px-Betty_White_in_The_Betty_White_Show_1954_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Betty_White_in_The_Betty_White_Show_1954_%282%29.jpg/330px-Betty_White_in_The_Betty_White_Show_1954_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Betty_White_in_The_Betty_White_Show_1954_%282%29.jpg/440px-Betty_White_in_The_Betty_White_Show_1954_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_in_The_Betty_White_Show_1954_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White in 1954</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1952, the same year that she began hosting <i>Hollywood on Television</i>, White co-founded Bandy Productions with writer <a href="/wiki/George_Tibbles" title="George Tibbles">George Tibbles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Don_Fedderson" title="Don Fedderson">Don Fedderson</a>, a producer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> The trio worked to create new shows using existing characters from sketches shown on <i>Hollywood on Television</i>. White, Fedderson, and Tibbles created the <a href="/wiki/Television_comedy" title="Television comedy">television comedy</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Life_with_Elizabeth" title="Life with Elizabeth">Life with Elizabeth</a></i>, with White portraying the <a href="/wiki/Title_role" title="Title role">title role</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> The show was originally a live production on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KLAC-TV" title="KLAC-TV">KLAC-TV</a> in 1951, and won White a <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Emmy_Award" title="Los Angeles Emmy Award">Regional Los Angeles Emmy</a> in 1952.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shemadeit_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-shemadeit-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneil20100617_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-oneil20100617-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Life with Elizabeth</i> was nationally <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_syndication" title="Broadcast syndication">syndicated</a> from 1952 to 1955, allowing White to become one of the few women in television with full creative control in front of and behind the camera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> The show was unusual for a sitcom in the 1950s because it was co-produced and owned by a twenty-eight-year-old woman who still lived with her parents. White said they didn't worry about relevance in those days, and that usually the incidents were based on real life situations that happened to her, the actor who played Alvin, and the writer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1954, she briefly hosted and produced her own daily talk show, <i>The Betty White Show</i>, on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> (not to be confused with her 1970s sitcom of the same name).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-7"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> Following <i>Life with Elizabeth</i>, she appeared as Vicki Angel on the sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Date_with_the_Angels" title="Date with the Angels">Date with the Angels</a></i> from 1957 to 1958. The show later became another variety series before going off the air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-8"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> White performed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commercials" title="Commercials">commercials</a> seen on live television in Los Angeles, including a rendition of the "Dr. Ross Dog Food" advertisement at <a href="/wiki/KTLA" title="KTLA">KTLA</a> during the 1950s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">1960s</span></h3>
<p>She made her feature film debut as Kansas Senator Elizabeth Ames Adams in the 1962 drama, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Advise_%26_Consent_(film)" title="Advise &amp; Consent (film)">Advise &amp; Consent</a></i>. Although her performance was well received, it would be her only big-screen appearance for decades.</p>
<p>Through the 1950s and 1960s, White began a nineteen-year run as hostess and commentator on the annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tournament_of_Roses_Parade" title="Tournament of Roses Parade">Tournament of Roses Parade</a> broadcast on NBC (often co-hosting with <a href="/wiki/Lorne_Greene" title="Lorne Greene">Lorne Greene</a>), and appeared on a number of late night talk shows and daytime game shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-9"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> White made many appearances on the hit game show <i><a href="/wiki/Password_(game_show)" title="Password (game show)">Password</a></i> as a celebrity guest from 1961 through 1975. She married the show's host, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Ludden" title="Allen Ludden">Allen Ludden</a>, in 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-10"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> She subsequently appeared on the show's three updated versions <i>Password Plus</i>, <i>Super Password</i>, and <i>Million Dollar Password</i>, having been on versions of the game with five different hosts (Allen Ludden, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Cullen" title="Bill Cullen">Bill Cullen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kennedy_(television_presenter)" title="Tom Kennedy (television presenter)">Tom Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bert_Convy" title="Bert Convy">Bert Convy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Regis_Philbin" title="Regis Philbin">Regis Philbin</a>). White made frequent game show appearances on <i><a href="/wiki/What%27s_My_Line%3F" title="What's My Line?">What's My Line?</a></i> (starting in 1955), <i><a href="/wiki/To_Tell_the_Truth" title="To Tell the Truth">To Tell the Truth</a></i> (in 1961, 1990, and 2015), <i><a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Got_a_Secret" title="I've Got a Secret">I've Got a Secret</a></i> (in 1972–73), <i>Match Game</i> (1973–1982), and <i><a href="/wiki/Pyramid_(game_show)" title="Pyramid (game show)">Pyramid</a></i> (starting in 1982). Both <i>Password</i> and <i>Pyramid</i> were created by White's friend, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Stewart_(television_producer)" title="Bob Stewart (television producer)">Bob Stewart</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_Sue_Ann_Nivens_1973.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="739" data-file-width="959" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Betty_White_Sue_Ann_Nivens_1973.JPG/220px-Betty_White_Sue_Ann_Nivens_1973.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Betty_White_Sue_Ann_Nivens_1973.JPG/330px-Betty_White_Sue_Ann_Nivens_1973.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Betty_White_Sue_Ann_Nivens_1973.JPG/440px-Betty_White_Sue_Ann_Nivens_1973.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_Sue_Ann_Nivens_1973.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White as Sue Ann Nivens in <i>The Mary Tyler Moore Show</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1973, White made several <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest appearances</a> in the fourth season of the CBS sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show" title="The Mary Tyler Moore Show">The Mary Tyler Moore Show</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-11"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> As a result of this appearance, she landed the regular role of the sardonic, man-hungry <a href="/wiki/Sue_Ann_Nivens" title="Sue Ann Nivens">Sue Ann Nivens</a>, "The Happy Homemaker", on the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-12"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> White would receive her second and third Emmys from her part on The Mary Tyler Moore Show. White considers her part as Sue Ann in the show one of the highlights of her professional career, but she describes her television image as "icky sweet." She felt that she was the very definition of feminine passivity, owing to the fact that White always seemed willing to satirize her own unique persona on screen in just such a way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Dell.2C_C._1997-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Running_gag" title="Running gag">running gag</a> was that Sue Ann's hard-edged private personality was the complete opposite of how she presented herself on her show. "We need somebody who can play sickeningly sweet, like Betty White," Moore herself suggested at a production meeting, which resulted in casting White herself. White won two Emmy Awards back-to-back for her role in the hugely popular series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-13"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show_cast_last_show_1977.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="757" data-file-width="963" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show_cast_last_show_1977.JPG/300px-Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show_cast_last_show_1977.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show_cast_last_show_1977.JPG/450px-Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show_cast_last_show_1977.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show_cast_last_show_1977.JPG/600px-Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show_cast_last_show_1977.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mary_Tyler_Moore_Show_cast_last_show_1977.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A scene from the final episode of the <i>Mary Tyler Moore Show</i> (<i>from left</i>): White, Gavin MacLeod, Ed Asner, Georgia Engel, Ted Knight, and Mary Tyler Moore</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1975, NBC replaced her as hostess and commentator on the Tournament of Roses Parade broadcast feeling she was too identified with rival network CBS due to her new found success on <i>The Mary Tyler Moore Show</i>. White admitted to <a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)"><i>People</i> magazine</a> it was difficult "watching someone else do my parade",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> although she soon would start a ten-year run as hostess of the <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s_Thanksgiving_Day_Parade" title="Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade">Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade</a> for CBS.</p>
<p>Following the end of <i>The Mary Tyler Moore Show</i> in 1977, White got her own sitcom on CBS, her second series entitled <i>The Betty White Show</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-14"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> (the first having been broadcast a quarter century earlier), during the 1977–78 season, in which she co-starred with <a href="/wiki/John_Hillerman" title="John Hillerman">John Hillerman</a> and former <i>Mary Tyler Moore</i> co-star <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Engel" title="Georgia Engel">Georgia Engel</a>. It was canceled after one season.</p>
<p>White appeared several times on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Carol_Burnett_Show" title="The Carol Burnett Show">The Carol Burnett Show</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Johnny_Carson" title="The Tonight Show Starring Johnny Carson">The Tonight Show Starring Johnny Carson</a></i> appearing in many sketches, and began guest-starring in a number of television movies and television miniseries, including <i><a href="/wiki/With_This_Ring_(TV_series)" title="With This Ring (TV series)">With This Ring</a></i>, <i>The Best Place to Be</i>, <i>Before and After</i>, and <i>The Gossip Columnist</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-15"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Girls_cast_miami_song.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="266" data-file-width="373" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/58/Golden_Girls_cast_miami_song.jpg/200px-Golden_Girls_cast_miami_song.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/58/Golden_Girls_cast_miami_song.jpg/300px-Golden_Girls_cast_miami_song.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/58/Golden_Girls_cast_miami_song.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Girls_cast_miami_song.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Main characters in the final scene from the season two episode "Big Daddy's Little Lady" (<i>from left</i>): Estelle Getty as Sophia, Rue McClanahan as Blanche, Betty White as Rose, and Beatrice Arthur as Dorothy</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1983, she became the first woman to win a <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award" title="Daytime Emmy Award">Daytime Emmy Award</a> in the category of Outstanding Game Show Host, for the NBC entry <i>Just Men!</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VanityFair_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-VanityFair-28">[28]</a></sup> Due to the amount of work she has done on them, she has been deemed the "First Lady of Game Shows".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1983 through 1985, she had a recurring role playing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ellen_Harper" title="Ellen Harper">Ellen Harper Jackson</a> on the series <i><a href="/wiki/Mama%27s_Family" title="Mama's Family">Mama's Family</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-16"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> along with future <i>Golden Girls</i> co-star Rue McClanahan. White had originated this character in a series of sketches on <i>The Carol Burnett Show</i> in the 1970s. When <i>Mama's Family</i> was picked up in <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_syndication" title="Broadcast syndication">syndication</a> after being canceled by NBC in 1985, White left the show (with the exception of one final appearance in the show's <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_syndication" title="Broadcast syndication">syndicated</a> version in 1986).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rose_Nylund.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="282" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/Rose_Nylund.jpg/180px-Rose_Nylund.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/Rose_Nylund.jpg/270px-Rose_Nylund.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/14/Rose_Nylund.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rose_Nylund.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White as Rose Nylund</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1985, White scored her second signature role and the biggest hit of her career as the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Nylund#St._Olaf" title="Rose Nylund">St. Olaf, Minnesota</a>-native <a href="/wiki/Rose_Nylund" title="Rose Nylund">Rose Nylund</a> on <i>The Golden Girls</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-17"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> The series chronicled the lives of four widowed or divorced women in their "golden years" who shared a home in Miami. <i>The Golden Girls</i>, which also starred <a href="/wiki/Bea_Arthur" title="Bea Arthur">Bea Arthur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estelle_Getty" title="Estelle Getty">Estelle Getty</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rue_McClanahan" title="Rue McClanahan">Rue McClanahan</a>, was immensely successful and ran from 1985 through 1992. White won one Emmy Award, for <i>Outstanding Actress in a Comedy Series</i>, for the first season of <i>The Golden Girls</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-18"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> and was nominated in that category every year of the show's run (the only cast member to receive that distinction – Getty was also nominated every year, but in the supporting actress category).</p>
<p>White was originally offered the role of Blanche in <i>The Golden Girls,</i> and Rue McClanahan was offered the role of Rose (the two characters being similar to roles they had played in <i>Mary Tyler Moore</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Maude_(TV_series)" title="Maude (TV series)">Maude</a></i>, respectively). <a href="/wiki/Jay_Sandrich" title="Jay Sandrich">Jay Sandrich</a>, the director of the pilot, suggested that since they had played similar roles in the past, they should switch roles, Rue McClanahan later said in a documentary on the series. White originally had doubts about her ability to play Rose, until the show's creator took her aside and told her not to play Rose as stupid but as someone "terminally naive, a person who always believed the first explanation of something."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span></h3>
<p>The show ended in 1992 after Arthur announced her decision to depart the series. White, McClanahan, and Getty reprised their roles Rose, Blanche, and Sophia in the spin-off <i><a href="/wiki/The_Golden_Palace" title="The Golden Palace">The Golden Palace</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-19"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> The series was short-lived, lasting only one season. In addition, White reprised her Rose Nylund character in guest appearances on the NBC shows <i><a href="/wiki/Empty_Nest" title="Empty Nest">Empty Nest</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Nurses_(TV_series)" title="Nurses (TV series)">Nurses</a></i>, both set in Miami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-20"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>After <i>The Golden Palace</i> ended,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-21"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> White guest-starred on a number of television programs including <i><a href="/wiki/Suddenly_Susan" title="Suddenly Susan">Suddenly Susan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Practice" title="The Practice">The Practice</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Yes,_Dear" title="Yes, Dear">Yes, Dear</a></i> where she received Emmy nominations for her individual appearances. She won an Emmy in 1996 for <i>Outstanding Guest Actress in a Comedy Series</i>, appearing as herself on an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_John_Larroquette_Show" title="The John Larroquette Show">The John Larroquette Show</a></i>. In that episode, titled "Here We Go Again", a <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">spoof</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Sunset_Boulevard_(film)" title="Sunset Boulevard (film)">Sunset Boulevard</a></i>, a diva-like White convinces Larroquette to help write her <a href="/wiki/Memoir" title="Memoir">memoirs</a>. At one point <i>Golden Girls</i> co-stars McClanahan and Getty appear as themselves. Larroquette is forced to dress in drag as Beatrice Arthur, when all four appear in public as the "original" cast members. White comically envisions her Rose as the central character with the others as mere supporting players.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_1989_Emmy_Awards.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1323" data-file-width="696" height="342" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Betty_White_1989_Emmy_Awards.jpg/180px-Betty_White_1989_Emmy_Awards.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Betty_White_1989_Emmy_Awards.jpg/270px-Betty_White_1989_Emmy_Awards.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Betty_White_1989_Emmy_Awards.jpg/360px-Betty_White_1989_Emmy_Awards.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_1989_Emmy_Awards.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White at the 1989 Emmy Awards</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span></h3>
<p>In December 2006, White joined the soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bold_and_the_Beautiful" title="The Bold and the Beautiful">The Bold and the Beautiful</a></i> in the role of Ann Douglas (where she would make 22 appearances), the long-lost mother of the show's matriarch, <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Forrester_(The_Bold_and_the_Beautiful)" title="Stephanie Forrester (The Bold and the Beautiful)">Stephanie Forrester</a>, played by <a href="/wiki/Susan_Flannery" title="Susan Flannery">Susan Flannery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007sow_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-2007sow-31">[31]</a></sup> She also began a recurring role in ABC's <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_Legal" title="Boston Legal">Boston Legal</a></i> from 2005 to 2008 as the calculating, blackmailing gossip-monger Catherine Piper, a role she originally played as a guest star on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Practice" title="The Practice">The Practice</a></i> in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-22"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>White appeared several times on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno">The Tonight Show with Jay Leno</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Show_with_Craig_Ferguson" title="The Late Late Show with Craig Ferguson">The Late Late Show with Craig Ferguson</a></i> appearing in many sketches and returned to <i>Password</i> in its latest incarnation, <i>Million Dollar Password</i>, on June 12, 2008, (episode #3), participating in the Million Dollar challenge at the end of the show. On May 19, 2008, she appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">The Oprah Winfrey Show</a></i>, taking part in the host's <i>Mary Tyler Moore Show</i> reunion special alongside every surviving cast member of the series.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BettyWhiteJune09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1698" data-file-width="1303" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BettyWhiteJune09.jpg/200px-BettyWhiteJune09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BettyWhiteJune09.jpg/300px-BettyWhiteJune09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BettyWhiteJune09.jpg/400px-BettyWhiteJune09.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BettyWhiteJune09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White at the premiere for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Proposal_(film)" title="The Proposal (film)">The Proposal</a></i> in June 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beginning in 2007, White was featured in television commercials for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PetMeds" title="PetMeds">PetMeds</a>, highlighting her interest in animal rights and welfare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span></h3>
<p>White appeared alongside <a href="/wiki/Abe_Vigoda" title="Abe Vigoda">Abe Vigoda</a> in an advertisement for <a href="/wiki/Snickers" title="Snickers">Snickers</a> during the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIV" title="Super Bowl XLIV">Super Bowl XLIV</a>. The ad won the top spot on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USA_Today_Super_Bowl_Ad_Meter" title="USA Today Super Bowl Ad Meter">USA Today Super Bowl Ad Meter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The slogan was, "You're not you when you're hungry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>A grassroots campaign on Facebook called "Betty White to Host SNL (Please)" began in January 2010. The group was approaching 500,000 members when NBC confirmed on March 11, 2010 that White would in fact host <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> on May 8. The appearance made her, at age 88, the oldest person to host the show, beating <a href="/wiki/Miskel_Spillman" title="Miskel Spillman">Miskel Spillman</a>, the winner of <i>SNL'</i>s "Anybody Can Host" contest, who was 80 when she hosted in 1977.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In her opening monologue, White thanked Facebook and joked that she "didn't know what Facebook was, and now that I do know what it is, I have to say, it sounds like a huge waste of time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNL2010_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-SNL2010-20">[20]</a></sup> The appearance earned her a 2010 Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Guest Actress in a Comedy Series, her seventh Emmy win overall.</p>
<p>In June 2010, White took on the role of Elka Ostrovsky the house caretaker on <a href="/wiki/TV_Land" title="TV Land">TV Land's</a> original sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Hot_in_Cleveland" title="Hot in Cleveland">Hot in Cleveland</a></i> along with <a href="/wiki/Valerie_Bertinelli" title="Valerie Bertinelli">Valerie Bertinelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Leeves" title="Jane Leeves">Jane Leeves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wendie_Malick" title="Wendie Malick">Wendie Malick</a>. <i>Hot in Cleveland</i> was TV Land's first attempt at a first-run scripted comedy (the channel has <a href="/wiki/Rerun" title="Rerun">rerun</a> other sitcoms since its debut). White was only meant to appear in the pilot of the show but was asked to stay on for the entire series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In 2011, she was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Supporting_Actress_in_a_Comedy_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Comedy Series">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Comedy Series</a> for her role as Elka, but lost to <a href="/wiki/Julie_Bowen" title="Julie Bowen">Julie Bowen</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Modern_Family" title="Modern Family">Modern Family</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HotInClevelandCastHWOFAug2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="799" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/HotInClevelandCastHWOFAug2012.jpg/400px-HotInClevelandCastHWOFAug2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/HotInClevelandCastHWOFAug2012.jpg/600px-HotInClevelandCastHWOFAug2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ea/HotInClevelandCastHWOFAug2012.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HotInClevelandCastHWOFAug2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Valerie_Bertinelli" title="Valerie Bertinelli">Valerie Bertinelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wendie_Malick" title="Wendie Malick">Wendie Malick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Leeves" title="Jane Leeves">Jane Leeves</a>, and <strong class="selflink">Betty White</strong> at a ceremony for Bertinelli to receive a star on the Hollywood Walk of Fame.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A Betty White calendar for 2011 was published in late 2010. The calendar features photos from White's career and with various animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> She also launched her own clothing line on July 22, 2010, which features shirts with her face on them. All proceeds go to various animal charities she supports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>White also starred in the <i><a href="/wiki/Hallmark_Hall_of_Fame" title="Hallmark Hall of Fame">Hallmark Hall of Fame</a></i> presentation of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_Valentine" title="The Lost Valentine">The Lost Valentine</a></i> on January 30, 2011. This presentation garnered the highest rating for a <i>Hallmark Hall of Fame</i> presentation in the last four years and according to the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Media_Research" title="Nielsen Media Research">Nielsen Media Research</a> TV rating service won first place in the prime time slot for that date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 2012 to 2014, White hosted and executive produced <i><a href="/wiki/Betty_White%27s_Off_Their_Rockers" title="Betty White's Off Their Rockers">Betty White's Off Their Rockers</a></i>, in which senior citizens play practical jokes on the younger generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> For this show, she received three Emmy nominations.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_and_Barack_Obama_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2731" data-file-width="4096" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Betty_White_and_Barack_Obama_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg/250px-Betty_White_and_Barack_Obama_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Betty_White_and_Barack_Obama_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg/375px-Betty_White_and_Barack_Obama_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Betty_White_and_Barack_Obama_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg/500px-Betty_White_and_Barack_Obama_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_and_Barack_Obama_in_the_Oval_Office.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White with <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">President Obama</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Oval_Office" title="Oval Office">Oval Office</a> in June 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A special <i>Betty White's 90th Birthday Party</i> aired on NBC a day before her birthday on January 16, 2012. The show featured appearances of many stars with whom White has worked over the years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> <i>Betty White's Off Their Rockers</i> aired following the celebratory event, and returned in April 2012 as a recurring show which resulted in an Emmy nomination for Outstanding Host for a Reality or Reality-Competition Program.</p>
<p>White's success continued in 2012 with her first Grammy Award for a spoken word recording for her best seller <i>If You Ask Me</i>. She also won the UCLA Jack Benny Award for Comedy, recognizing her significant contribution to comedy in television, and was <a href="/wiki/Roast_(comedy)" title="Roast (comedy)">roasted</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Friars%27_Club" title="New York Friars' Club">New York Friars' Club</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In January 2013, NBC once again celebrated Betty White's birthday with a TV special featuring celebrity friends, including former president <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>; the special aired on February 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Allen_Ludden_Betty_White1968.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="821" data-file-width="670" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Allen_Ludden_Betty_White1968.JPG/180px-Allen_Ludden_Betty_White1968.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Allen_Ludden_Betty_White1968.JPG/270px-Allen_Ludden_Betty_White1968.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Allen_Ludden_Betty_White1968.JPG/360px-Allen_Ludden_Betty_White1968.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Allen_Ludden_Betty_White1968.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White and Ludden in 1968.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1945, White married Dick Barker, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army_Air_Corps" title="U.S. Army Air Corps">U.S. Army Air Corps</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilot_(aircraft)" title="Pilot (aircraft)">pilot</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-People19_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-People19-46">[46]</a></sup> The marriage was short-lived. In 1947, she married Lane Allen, a Hollywood <a href="/wiki/Talent_agent" title="Talent agent">agent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-People19_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-People19-46">[46]</a></sup> This marriage ended in divorce in 1949.</p>
<p>On June 14, 1963, White married television host and personality <a href="/wiki/Allen_Ludden" title="Allen Ludden">Allen Ludden</a>, whom she had met on his game show <i>Password</i> as a celebrity guest in 1961,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and her legal name was changed to Betty White Ludden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BiographyCom_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-BiographyCom-2">[2]</a></sup> He proposed to White at least twice before she accepted. The couple appeared together in an episode of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Odd_Couple_(TV_series)" title="The Odd Couple (TV series)">The Odd Couple</a></i> featuring Felix's and Oscar's appearance on <i>Password</i>. Ludden appeared as a guest panelist on <i>Match Game</i>, with White sitting in the audience. (She was prompted to criticize one of Ludden's wrong answers on camera during an episode of <i>Match Game '74</i>.) The two appeared together on the <i>Match Game</i> panel in 1974, 1975 and 1980.</p>
<p>Allen Ludden died from <a href="/wiki/Stomach_cancer" title="Stomach cancer">stomach cancer</a> on June 9, 1981, in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inside_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Inside-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> They had no children together, though she is stepmother to his three children from his first marriage, when his wife had died. White has not remarried since Ludden's death. In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Larry_King_Live" title="Larry King Live">Larry King</a>, when asked whether she would remarry, she replied by saying "Once you've had the best, who needs the rest?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Friendships">Friendships</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bea_Arthur">Bea Arthur</span></h4>
<p>White had a strained relationship with her <i>Golden Girls</i> co-star <a href="/wiki/Bea_Arthur" title="Bea Arthur">Bea Arthur</a> on and off the set of their television show, commenting that Arthur "was not fond of her" and that "she found me a pain in the neck sometimes. It was my positive attitude and that made Bea mad sometimes. Sometimes if I was happy, she'd be furious." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bea_Arthur_was_not_fond_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bea_Arthur_was_not_fond-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> After Arthur's death in 2009, White said, "I knew it would hurt, I just didn't know it would hurt this much."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberace">Liberace</span></h4>
<p>In a 2011 interview, White said that she always knew her close friend <a href="/wiki/Liberace" title="Liberace">Liberace</a> was gay and that she sometimes accompanied him to premieres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bea_Arthur_was_not_fond_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bea_Arthur_was_not_fond-51">[51]</a></sup> A supporter of gay rights, White said that "If a couple has been together all that time – and there are gay relationships that are more solid than some heterosexual ones – I think it's fine if they want to get married. I don't know how people can get so anti-something. Mind your own business, take care of your affairs, and don't worry about other people so much".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mary_Tyler_Moore">Mary Tyler Moore</span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mary_Tyler_Moore" title="Mary Tyler Moore">Mary Tyler Moore</a>, and her then-husband <a href="/wiki/Grant_Tinker" title="Grant Tinker">Grant Tinker</a> were close friends with White and Ludden. When <a href="/wiki/Valerie_Harper" title="Valerie Harper">Valerie Harper</a> left <i>The Mary Tyler Moore Show</i> producers felt the show needed another female character and created Sue Ann Nivens in the process. Nivens was described as an "icky sweet Betty White type", but they went against asking White to audition. In a 2010 <a href="/wiki/Archive_of_American_Television" title="Archive of American Television">Archive of American Television</a> interview, Moore explained that producers, aware of Moore and White's friendship, were initially hesitant to audition White for the role, the fear being that if she hadn't been right, that it would create awkwardness between the two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_work">Humanitarian work</span></h3>
<p>White is a pet enthusiast and animal health <a href="/wiki/Advocate" title="Advocate">advocate</a> who works with a number of animal organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Zoo" title="Los Angeles Zoo">Los Angeles Zoo</a> Commission, the <a href="/wiki/Morris_Animal_Foundation" title="Morris Animal Foundation">Morris Animal Foundation</a>, African Wildlife Foundation, and Actors &amp; Others for Animals. Her interest in <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a> and welfare began in the early 1970s while she was both producing and hosting the syndicated series, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Pet_Set&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Pet Set (page does not exist)">The Pet Set</a></i>, which spotlighted celebrities and their pets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-23"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2009, White is the president <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">emerita</a> of the Morris Animal Foundation, where she has served as a <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustee</a> of the organization since 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-24"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> She has been a member of the board of directors of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Los_Angeles_Zoo_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Greater Los Angeles Zoo Association (page does not exist)">Greater Los Angeles Zoo Association</a> since 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-25"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> Additionally, White served the zoo association as a Zoo Commissioner for eight years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-26"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the Los Angeles Zoo &amp; Botanical Garden's "ZooScape" Member Newsletter, White hosted "History on Film" from 2000 to 2002. White donated nearly $100,000 to the zoo in the month of April 2008 alone.</p>
<p>Betty White served as a presenter at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/American_Humane_Association" title="American Humane Association">American Humane Association</a> Hero Dog Awards ceremony at <a href="/wiki/The_Beverly_Hilton" title="The Beverly Hilton">The Beverly Hilton</a> Hotel on October 1, 2011, in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2011, she teamed up with English singer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luciana_(entertainer)" title="Luciana (entertainer)">Luciana</a> to produce a remix of her song "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Still_Hot" title="I'm Still Hot">I'm Still Hot</a>". The song was released digitally on September 22 and the video later premiered on October 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> It was made for a campaign for a life settlement program, The Lifeline. White served as a judge alongside <a href="/wiki/Whoopi_Goldberg" title="Whoopi Goldberg">Whoopi Goldberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Diamond" title="Wendy Diamond">Wendy Diamond</a> for the <a href="/wiki/American_Humane_Association" title="American Humane Association">American Humane Association's</a> Hero Dog Awards airing on The Hallmark Channel on November 8, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Veterinary_Medical_Association" title="American Veterinary Medical Association">American Veterinary Medical Association</a> awarded White with its Humane Award in 1987 for her charitable work with animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-27"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> The City of Los Angeles further honored her for her philanthropic work with animals in 2006 with a <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a> <a href="/wiki/Commemorative_plaque" title="Commemorative plaque">plaque</a> near the Gorilla Exhibit at the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Zoo" title="Los Angeles Zoo">Los Angeles Zoo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-28"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> The City of Los Angeles named her "Ambassador to the Animals" at the dedication ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-29"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_1988_Emmy_Awards_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1037" data-file-width="726" height="314" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Betty_White_1988_Emmy_Awards_2.jpg/220px-Betty_White_1988_Emmy_Awards_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Betty_White_1988_Emmy_Awards_2.jpg/330px-Betty_White_1988_Emmy_Awards_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Betty_White_1988_Emmy_Awards_2.jpg/440px-Betty_White_1988_Emmy_Awards_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White_1988_Emmy_Awards_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White at the 1988 Emmy Awards</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>She was formally inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Television_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences">Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hall_of_Fame" title="Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> in 1995. In 2009, White received the <a href="/wiki/TCA_Career_Achievement_Award" title="TCA Career Achievement Award">TCA Career Achievement Award</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Television_Critics_Association" title="Television Critics Association">Television Critics Association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-30"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a> (SAG) announced plans to honor White with the Screen Actors Guild Life Achievement Award at the <a href="/wiki/16th_Screen_Actors_Guild_Awards" title="16th Screen Actors Guild Awards">16th Screen Actors Guild Awards</a>. Actress <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Bullock" title="Sandra Bullock">Sandra Bullock</a> presented White with the award on January 23, 2010, at the ceremony, which took place at the <a href="/wiki/Shrine_Auditorium" title="Shrine Auditorium">Shrine Auditorium</a> in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-31"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> She is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kentucky_Colonel" title="Kentucky Colonel">Kentucky Colonel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In 2009, White and her now-deceased <i>Golden Girls</i> cast mates Bea Arthur, Rue McClanahan, and Estelle Getty were awarded honorary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney_Legend" title="Disney Legend">Disney Legend</a> awards. Betty was inducted into the California Hall of Fame in December 2010. In 2010 she was chosen as the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>'s Entertainer of the Year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Golden_Girls_Disney_Legends.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1872" data-file-width="1766" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/The_Golden_Girls_Disney_Legends.jpg/220px-The_Golden_Girls_Disney_Legends.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/The_Golden_Girls_Disney_Legends.jpg/330px-The_Golden_Girls_Disney_Legends.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/The_Golden_Girls_Disney_Legends.jpg/440px-The_Golden_Girls_Disney_Legends.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Golden_Girls_Disney_Legends.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Golden Girls <a href="/wiki/Disney_Legends" title="Disney Legends">Disney Legends</a> plaque at <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(Burbank)" title="Walt Disney Studios (Burbank)">Walt Disney Studios</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On November 9, 2010, the USDA Forest Service, along with <a href="/wiki/Smokey_Bear" title="Smokey Bear">Smokey Bear</a>, made Betty White an honorary forest ranger, fulfilling her lifelong dream.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> White said in previous interviews that she wanted to be a forest ranger as a little girl but that women were not allowed to do that then. When White received the honor, more than one-third of Forest Service employees were women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2011, White was awarded an honorary degree and white doctors coat by <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_University" title="Washington State University">Washington State University</a> at the Washington State Veterinary Medical Association's centennial gala in <a href="/wiki/Yakima,_Washington" title="Yakima, Washington">Yakima, Washington</a>.</p>
<p>A 2011 poll conducted by <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ipsos" title="Ipsos">Ipsos</a> revealed that White was considered the most popular and most trusted celebrity among Americans, beating the likes of <a href="/wiki/Denzel_Washington" title="Denzel Washington">Denzel Washington</a>, Sandra Bullock, and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Betty_White" title="List of awards and nominations received by Betty White">List of awards and nominations received by Betty White</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White%27s_Star_HWF.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2273" data-file-width="1944" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Betty_White%27s_Star_HWF.JPG/200px-Betty_White%27s_Star_HWF.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Betty_White%27s_Star_HWF.JPG/300px-Betty_White%27s_Star_HWF.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Betty_White%27s_Star_HWF.JPG/400px-Betty_White%27s_Star_HWF.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betty_White%27s_Star_HWF.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Walk of Fame</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>White is the only woman to have received an Emmy in all performing comedic categories, and also holds the record for longest span between Emmy nominations for performances—her first was in 1951 and her most recent was in 2011, a span of 60 years. She is the fourth oldest winner of a competitive <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> and the oldest nominee of a performing Emmy<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<p>White has won five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="Primetime Emmy Awards">Primetime Emmy Awards</a>, two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Awards" title="Daytime Emmy Awards">Daytime Emmy Awards</a> (including the 2015 Daytime Emmy for Lifetime Achievement), and received a <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Emmy_Award" title="Los Angeles Emmy Award">Regional (LA) Emmy</a> in 1952. She has also won three <a href="/wiki/American_Comedy_Awards" title="American Comedy Awards">American Comedy Awards</a> (including a Lifetime Achievement Award in 1990), and two <a href="/wiki/Viewers_for_Quality_Television" title="Viewers for Quality Television">Viewers for Quality Television</a> Awards. She was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Television_Hall_of_Fame" title="Television Hall of Fame">Television Hall of Fame</a> in 1995 and has a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> at <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Boulevard" title="Hollywood Boulevard">6747 Hollywood Boulevard</a> alongside the star of her late husband Allen Ludden.</p>
<p>White was the recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Pioneer_Broadcasters" title="Pacific Pioneer Broadcasters">Pacific Pioneer Broadcasters</a> Golden Ike Award and the Genii Award from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Women_in_Radio_and_Television" title="American Women in Radio and Television">American Women in Radio and Television</a> in 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-32"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup> The American Comedy Awards awarded her the award for Funniest Female in 1987 as well as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Lifetime Achievement Award">Lifetime Achievement Award</a> in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thr_4-33"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2011, White received a SAG Award for Outstanding Performance by a Female Actor in a Comedy Series for her role as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elka_Ostrovsky" title="Elka Ostrovsky">Elka Ostrovsky</a> in <i>Hot in Cleveland</i>. The show itself was also nominated for an award as Outstanding Performance by an Ensemble in a Comedy Series, but lost to the cast of <i><a href="/wiki/Modern_Family" title="Modern Family">Modern Family</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> She won the same award again in 2012, and has received a third nomination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h2>
<p>White has published several books during her career. In August 2010, she entered a deal with G.P. Putnam's Sons to produce two more books, the first of which, <i>If You Ask Me (And of Course You Won't)</i>, was released in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In February 2012, White received her first <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> ("Best Spoken Word Recording") for the audio recording of the book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>

<tr>

<th>Title</th>

<td></td>

<td></td>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="background: #BDB76B">British Artist of the Year</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-even hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
